  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f878be09-9be0-441a-b550-448f35b7b78f'
      });

              <span id="reviewTextContainer458937890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7137710556355517796">I love John Green, but I feel like the only 13 year old who does! Is there anyone else out there? I read The Fault in Our Stars and I decided right then and there that I would stalk him this summer and yell at him for what happened to Augustus. Nevertheless, he is awesome and I would love to meet him one day.</span>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5254085274013849429">I’m just going to talk about these all at once (Will Grayson, Will Grayson. Paper Towns. The Fault in Our Stars. An Abundance of Katherines.), since I read them all in the span of about a week….<br/><br/>Let me set the scene. I read “Looking for Alaska” a while ago, and after I read and dug it, I bought the rest of his books for my kindle almost immediately. Of these four, I started with TFiOS. I thought to myself, “It’s about 8pm on a Saturday night, Hubby is hunkered down playing videogames, I might as </span>
  <span id="freeText5254085274013849429" style="display:none">I’m just going to talk about these all at once (Will Grayson, Will Grayson. Paper Towns. The Fault in Our Stars. An Abundance of Katherines.), since I read them all in the span of about a week….<br /><br />Let me set the scene. I read “Looking for Alaska” a while ago, and after I read and dug it, I bought the rest of his books for my kindle almost immediately. Of these four, I started with TFiOS. I thought to myself, “It’s about 8pm on a Saturday night, Hubby is hunkered down playing videogames, I might as well start a new book.” <br /><br />This was either the best thing or the worst thing I have ever done. <br /><br />I read TFiOS in one sitting, from 8pm to after 4am. Hubby kept looking over at me when I had a steady stream of tears and snot coming down my face, sniffling loudly (it sounded like this: *snooooorrrrrkkkkkkkkkk*) and blowing my nose with the Chipotle napkins left from dinner since I didn’t want to step out of the story to go get actual tissues. I was a hot mess. A. Hot. Mess. Getting out of bed for Sunday lunch with my parents was not fun for either of us.<br /><br />I haven’t cried like that in a long, long time… since March 15, 2009, actually. It was a real catharsis, one that I didn’t know I needed.<br /><br />I powered through the other three very quickly, and I enjoyed them a lot. I didn’t have as visceral of a reaction to them as I did to TFiOS, but I dug them. <br /><br />All four are highly recommended, but TFiOS most of all… though not on a work or school night… :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5254085274013849429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3622349494994192430">First review, this might be bad x)<br/>All of John Green's books are great, in my opinion. I've always found him to be one of the more constant authors out there, and one of my favorites. But I've also seen constant patterns in his books. Examples: a broken-down car and a "psychopathic" type of driver. An extremely hot, sexy girl (or boy, in the case of TFiOS). Sometimes it gets a bit tiring to read the same type of book over and over again, but with John Green, even though his books have many simila</span>
  <span id="freeText3622349494994192430" style="display:none">First review, this might be bad x)<br />All of John Green's books are great, in my opinion. I've always found him to be one of the more constant authors out there, and one of my favorites. But I've also seen constant patterns in his books. Examples: a broken-down car and a "psychopathic" type of driver. An extremely hot, sexy girl (or boy, in the case of TFiOS). Sometimes it gets a bit tiring to read the same type of book over and over again, but with John Green, even though his books have many similarities, each of them is also unique in each of their different ways. It is these factors that make me enjoy his books more than authors who have recurring themes in their books. And that concludes my slight failure of a review, as I am off to do homework!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare" href="/user/show/4927816-clare">Clare</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer913026845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12351028949011440697">If you have a chance to get this box set, it's quite worth it. Shop around a little, read all the seller's descriptions VERY carefully, and write down how they advertised it (so if you don't get what they SAID they'd sell you you can reference their words back to them when you write back and ask why they didn't honor their ad.) Amazon has very good support so, quite worth the effort to find a good offer. :) And these are REALLY well written books.<br/><br/>Parents, if you have children that you want to re</span>
  <span id="freeText12351028949011440697" style="display:none">If you have a chance to get this box set, it's quite worth it. Shop around a little, read all the seller's descriptions VERY carefully, and write down how they advertised it (so if you don't get what they SAID they'd sell you you can reference their words back to them when you write back and ask why they didn't honor their ad.) Amazon has very good support so, quite worth the effort to find a good offer. :) And these are REALLY well written books.<br /><br />Parents, if you have children that you want to read books that will inspire them to look beyond the surface-- learn to feel empathy for other people-- think about higher issues, like life after death, what is it like when a teenager gets cancer? <br /><br />Can a teen who has cancer who falls in love with their true love experience a piece of their 'infinity'--Now-- as a young person? Can they seek fulfillment, and purpose in the short time they have? <br /><br />Do we always know why we love someone? Is our idea of why we love them always right? <br /><br />If you think these are GOOD QUESTIONS for your kids to be asking themselves (I sure as heck do)-- buy this set, or get these books from the library. <br /><br />John Green writes about who Teenagers are. He also has a Vlog series on the web with his brother where they talk to each other, and answer fan questions: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/user/vlogbrothers">www.youtube.com/user/vlogbrothers</a><br />, an educational series, <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/user/crashcourse">www.youtube.com/user/crashcourse</a>‎<br />he often hosts Mental Floss, a Youtube show that gives odd, but useful information: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/user/MentalFlossVideo">www.youtube.com/user/MentalFlossVideo</a>‎<br /><br />Last I looked, Mr. Green had 5 out of the New York Times, Best Sellers List, Young Adult Hard Cover Books. <br /><br />Would I want my child exposed to John Green? Well, only if I want them to model themselves after someone who is funny, open minded, extremely intelligent, honestly likes young people and respects them and WANTS them to learn and respect themselves.<br /><br />So, oh.. yes please! My girls can watch both the Green brother's videos and read John Green's books all they want.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12351028949011440697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_537340398" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537340398" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4045913-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425733118p2/4045913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537340398?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/4045913-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537340398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1931554673441217085">John Green is a powerhouse writer and one of the best in YA. He manages to create realistic stories with both humour and heart. The characters are authentic and the humour comes naturally. <br/><br/>My favourite book of his is The Fault in Our Stars. It is a near perfect book and will remain iconic in YA for generations to come. <br/><br/>My second favourite is An Abundance of Katherines. It has a weird blurb but it is a hilarious story. I found myself laughing aloud dozens of times while reading this novel. <br/><br/>Paper </span>
  <span id="freeText1931554673441217085" style="display:none">John Green is a powerhouse writer and one of the best in YA. He manages to create realistic stories with both humour and heart. The characters are authentic and the humour comes naturally. <br /><br />My favourite book of his is The Fault in Our Stars. It is a near perfect book and will remain iconic in YA for generations to come. <br /><br />My second favourite is An Abundance of Katherines. It has a weird blurb but it is a hilarious story. I found myself laughing aloud dozens of times while reading this novel. <br /><br />Paper Towns is my third favourite story. It is very funny and a mystery. <br /><br />Looking for Alaska, while my least favourite of his works is still very good. The reason Looking for Alaska and Paper Towns are my least favourites is because I find the main female characters (Alaska and Margo) annoying. Although this is arguably the point of both novels (to break down the illusion of the manic pixie dream girl) it decreased my enjoyment of the novel. Having said that they are both 4 star books and definitely worth reading. <br /><br />A John Green novel is a must read and guaranteed to be excellent. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1931554673441217085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText519481381051670620" style="display:none">This review is for the book <u>Papertowns</u> by John Green. The beginning was amazing, totally hooked me in, loved the intrigue and the idea of the scavenger hunt that Margot was sending Q on. Unfortunately, by the end of the book I was over it. I felt like the story petered out and I just wanted it to be over. When I read <u>The Fault in Our Stars</u> I literally could not put the book down. That story hooked me from beginning to end without letting up on the intensity. This story just fell flat after awhile which was a disappointment. I gave it three stars because the beginning was well done and the idea was interesting.</span>

The four books are truly a wonder that people who love fictional literature should read. Though the endings of some, may cause people to differ from others. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gHBriKrgYxcaXv8JeVIQLOOnIn+P4oDoMKc1jZQRaq1m+cgbykwZnI1ZwAK57OI7WNKzUprGOiWv/DNUduEWbQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YwDqV3y43BnUtmKSXwOcU4GmE6bWT01u/OqFN1OnYeyFiUnEHBSmkkOxXZmfvW5EOtOCi8Nr96NjsYPusVcdLA==')})
  }

When Lily Hayes arrives in Buenos Aires for her semester abroad, she is enchanted by everything she encounters: the colorful buildings, the street food, the handsome, elusive man next door. Her studious roommate Katy is a bit of a bore, but Lily didn’t come to Argentina to hang out with other Americans.   Five weeks later, Katy is found brutally murdered in their shared home, and Lily is the prime suspect. But who is Lily Hayes? It depends on who’s asking. As the case takes shape—revealing deceptions, secrets, and suspicious DNA—Lily appears alternately sinister and guileless through the eyes of those around her: the media, her family, the man who loves her and the man who seeks her conviction. With mordant wit and keen emotional insight, Cartwheel offers a prismatic investigation of the ways we decide what to see—and to believe—in one another and ourselves.   Jennifer duBois’s debut novel, A Partial History of Lost Causes, was a finalist for the PEN/Hemingway Award for Debut Fiction and was honored by the National Book Foundation’s 5 Under 35 program. In Cartwheel, duBois delivers a novel of propulsive psychological suspense and rare moral nuance. Who is Lily Hayes? What happened to her roommate? No two readers will agree.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1406384.John_Green">About John Green</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1406384.John_Green"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1353452301p3/1406384.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1406384.John_Green">John Green
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17595012646158427779"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>John Green's first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska' title='Looking for Alaska by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Looking for Alaska</a>, won the 2006 Michael L. Printz Award presented by the American Library Association. His second novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49750.An_Abundance_of_Katherines' title='An Abundance of Katherines by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Abundance of Katherines</a>, was a 2007 Michael L. Printz Award Honor Book and a finalist for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize. His next novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2914097.Paper_Towns' title='Paper Towns by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paper Towns</a>, is a New </span>
  <span id="freeText17595012646158427779" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />John Green's first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/99561.Looking_for_Alaska" title="Looking for Alaska by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alaska</a>, won the 2006 Michael L. Printz Award presented by the American Library Association. His second novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49750.An_Abundance_of_Katherines" title="An Abundance of Katherines by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">An Abundance of Katherines</a>, was a 2007 Michael L. Printz Award Honor Book and a finalist for the Los Angeles Times Book Prize. His next novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2914097.Paper_Towns" title="Paper Towns by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a>, is a New York Times bestseller and won the Edgar Allen Poe Award for Best YA Mystery. In January 2012, his most recent novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a>, was met with wide critical acclaim, unprecedented in Green's career. The praise included rave reviews in Time Magazine and The New York Times, on NPR, and from award-winning author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11466.Markus_Zusak" title="Markus Zusak" rel="nofollow noopener">Markus Zusak</a>. The book also topped the New York Times Children's Paperback Bestseller list for several weeks. Green has also coauthored a book with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" title="David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a>, published in 2010. The film rights for all his books, with the exception of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson Will Grayson</a>, have been optioned to major Hollywood Studios.<br /><br />In 2007, John and his brother Hank were the hosts of a popular internet blog, "<a href="http://www.brotherhood2.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Brotherhood 2.0</a>," where they discussed their lives, books and current events every day for a year except for weekends and holidays. They still keep a video blog, now called "The Vlog Brothers," which can be found on the <a href="http://nerdfighters.ning.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Nerdfighters</a> website, or a direct link <a href="http://youtube.com/vlogbrothers" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17595012646158427779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
